    <h2>Python OOPS Interview Questions</h2>

        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="how-to-create-a-class-in-python">
          <h3>39. How do you create a class in Python?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>To create a class in python, we use the keyword class as shown in the example below:</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-class"><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">InterviewbitEmployee</span>:</span>
   <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">__init__</span>(<span class="hljs-params">self, emp_name</span>):</span>
       self.emp_name = emp_name</code></pre><p>To instantiate or create an object from the class created above, we do the following:</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs">emp_1=InterviewbitEmployee(<span class="hljs-string">"Mr. Employee"</span>)</code></pre><p>To access the name attribute, we just call the attribute using the dot operator as shown below:</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(emp_1.emp_name)
<span class="hljs-comment"># Prints Mr. Employee</span></code></pre><p>To create methods inside the class, we include the methods under the scope of the class as shown below:</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-class"><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">InterviewbitEmployee</span>:</span>
   <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">__init__</span>(<span class="hljs-params">self, emp_name</span>):</span>
       self.emp_name = emp_name

   <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">introduce</span>(<span class="hljs-params">self</span>):</span>
       <span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"Hello I am "</span> + self.emp_name)</code></pre><p>The self parameter in the init and introduce functions represent the reference to the current class instance which is used for accessing attributes and methods of that class. The self parameter has to be the first parameter of any method defined inside the class. The method of the class InterviewbitEmployee can be accessed as shown below:</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs">emp_1.introduce()</code></pre><p>The overall program would look like this:</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-class"><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">InterviewbitEmployee</span>:</span>
   <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">__init__</span>(<span class="hljs-params">self, emp_name</span>):</span>
       self.emp_name = emp_name

   <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">introduce</span>(<span class="hljs-params">self</span>):</span>
       <span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"Hello I am "</span> + self.emp_name)

<span class="hljs-comment"># create an object of InterviewbitEmployee class</span>
emp_1 = InterviewbitEmployee(<span class="hljs-string">"Mr Employee"</span>)
<span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(emp_1.emp_name)    <span class="hljs-comment">#print employee name</span>
emp_1.introduce()        <span class="hljs-comment">#introduce the employee</span></code></pre>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="inheritance-in-python">
          <h3>40. How does inheritance work in python? Explain it with an example.</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>Inheritance gives the power to a class to access all attributes and methods of another class. It aids in code reusability and helps the developer to maintain applications without redundant code. The class inheriting from another class is a child class or also called a derived class. The class from which a child class derives the members are called parent class or superclass.</p><p>Python supports different kinds of inheritance, they are:</p><ul><li>
<strong>Single Inheritance</strong>: Child class derives members of one parent class.</li></ul><figure class="image image_resized" style="width:75%;"><img data-src="https://s3.ap-south-1.amazonaws.com/myinterviewtrainer-domestic/public_assets/assets/000/000/928/original/Single_Inheritance.jpg?1629984086" class="lazy-elem"></figure><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-comment"># Parent class</span>
<span class="hljs-class"><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">ParentClass</span>:</span>
    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">par_func</span>(<span class="hljs-params">self</span>):</span>
         <span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"I am parent class function"</span>)

<span class="hljs-comment"># Child class</span>
<span class="hljs-class"><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">ChildClass</span>(<span class="hljs-params">ParentClass</span>):</span>
    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">child_func</span>(<span class="hljs-params">self</span>):</span>
         <span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"I am child class function"</span>)

<span class="hljs-comment"># Driver code</span>
obj1 = ChildClass()
obj1.par_func()
obj1.child_func()</code></pre><ul><li>
<strong>Multi-level Inheritance: </strong>The members of the parent class, A, are inherited by child class which is then inherited by another child class, B. The features of the base class and the derived class are further inherited into the new derived class, C. Here, A is the grandfather class of class C.</li></ul><figure class="image image_resized" style="width:75%;"><img data-src="https://s3.ap-south-1.amazonaws.com/myinterviewtrainer-domestic/public_assets/assets/000/000/930/original/Multi-level_Inheritance.jpg?1629984200" class="lazy-elem"></figure><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-comment"># Parent class</span>
<span class="hljs-class"><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">A</span>:</span>
   <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">__init__</span>(<span class="hljs-params">self, a_name</span>):</span>
       self.a_name = a_name

<span class="hljs-comment"># Intermediate class</span>
<span class="hljs-class"><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">B</span>(<span class="hljs-params">A</span>):</span>
   <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">__init__</span>(<span class="hljs-params">self, b_name, a_name</span>):</span>
       self.b_name = b_name
       <span class="hljs-comment"># invoke constructor of class A</span>
       A.__init__(self, a_name)

<span class="hljs-comment"># Child class</span>
<span class="hljs-class"><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">C</span>(<span class="hljs-params">B</span>):</span>
   <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">__init__</span>(<span class="hljs-params">self,c_name, b_name, a_name</span>):</span>
       self.c_name = c_name
       <span class="hljs-comment"># invoke constructor of class B</span>
       B.__init__(self, b_name, a_name)

   <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">display_names</span>(<span class="hljs-params">self</span>):</span>
       <span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"A name : "</span>, self.a_name)
       <span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"B name : "</span>, self.b_name)
       <span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"C name : "</span>, self.c_name)

<span class="hljs-comment">#  Driver code</span>
obj1 = C(<span class="hljs-string">'child'</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'intermediate'</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'parent'</span>)
<span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(obj1.a_name)
obj1.display_names()
 </code></pre><ul><li>
<strong>Multiple Inheritance:</strong> This is achieved when one child class derives members from more than one parent class. All features of parent classes are inherited in the child class.</li></ul><figure class="image image_resized" style="width:75%;"><img data-src="https://s3.ap-south-1.amazonaws.com/myinterviewtrainer-domestic/public_assets/assets/000/000/934/original/Multiple_Inheritance.jpg?1629984498" class="lazy-elem"></figure><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-comment"># Parent class1</span>
<span class="hljs-class"><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">Parent1</span>:</span>
   <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">parent1_func</span>(<span class="hljs-params">self</span>):</span>
       <span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"Hi I am first Parent"</span>)

<span class="hljs-comment"># Parent class2</span>
<span class="hljs-class"><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">Parent2</span>:</span>
   <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">parent2_func</span>(<span class="hljs-params">self</span>):</span>
       <span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"Hi I am second Parent"</span>)

<span class="hljs-comment"># Child class</span>
<span class="hljs-class"><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">Child</span>(<span class="hljs-params">Parent1, Parent2</span>):</span>
   <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">child_func</span>(<span class="hljs-params">self</span>):</span>
       self.parent1_func()
       self.parent2_func()

<span class="hljs-comment"># Driver's code</span>
obj1 = Child()
obj1.child_func()</code></pre><ul><li>
<strong>Hierarchical Inheritance: </strong>When a parent class is derived by more than one child class, it is called hierarchical inheritance.</li></ul><figure class="image image_resized" style="width:75%;"><img data-src="https://s3.ap-south-1.amazonaws.com/myinterviewtrainer-domestic/public_assets/assets/000/000/935/original/Hierarchical_Inheritance.jpg?1629985141" class="lazy-elem"></figure><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-comment"># Base class</span>
<span class="hljs-class"><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">A</span>:</span>
     <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">a_func</span>(<span class="hljs-params">self</span>):</span>
         <span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"I am from the parent class."</span>)

<span class="hljs-comment"># 1st Derived class</span>
<span class="hljs-class"><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">B</span>(<span class="hljs-params">A</span>):</span>
     <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">b_func</span>(<span class="hljs-params">self</span>):</span>
         <span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"I am from the first child."</span>)

<span class="hljs-comment"># 2nd Derived class</span>
<span class="hljs-class"><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">C</span>(<span class="hljs-params">A</span>):</span>
     <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">c_func</span>(<span class="hljs-params">self</span>):</span>
         <span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"I am from the second child."</span>)

<span class="hljs-comment"># Driver's code</span>
obj1 = B()
obj2 = C()
obj1.a_func()
obj1.b_func()    <span class="hljs-comment">#child 1 method</span>
obj2.a_func()
obj2.c_func()    <span class="hljs-comment">#child 2 method</span></code></pre>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="how-do-you-access-parent-members-in-the-child-class">
          <h3>41. How do you access parent members in the child class?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>Following are the ways using which you can access parent class members within a child class:</p><ul><li>
<strong>By using Parent class name:</strong> You can use the name of the parent class to access the attributes as shown in the example below:</li></ul><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-class"><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">Parent</span>(<span class="hljs-params"><span class="hljs-built_in">object</span></span>):</span>
   <span class="hljs-comment"># Constructor</span>
   <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">__init__</span>(<span class="hljs-params">self, name</span>):</span>
       self.name = name

<span class="hljs-class"><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">Child</span>(<span class="hljs-params">Parent</span>):</span>
   <span class="hljs-comment"># Constructor</span>
   <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">__init__</span>(<span class="hljs-params">self, name, age</span>):</span>
       Parent.name = name
       self.age = age

   <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">display</span>(<span class="hljs-params">self</span>):</span>
       <span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(Parent.name, self.age)

<span class="hljs-comment"># Driver Code</span>
obj = Child(<span class="hljs-string">"Interviewbit"</span>, <span class="hljs-number">6</span>)
obj.display()</code></pre><ul><li>
<strong>By using super():</strong> The parent class members can be accessed in child class using the super keyword.</li></ul><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-class"><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">Parent</span>(<span class="hljs-params"><span class="hljs-built_in">object</span></span>):</span>
   <span class="hljs-comment"># Constructor</span>
   <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">__init__</span>(<span class="hljs-params">self, name</span>):</span>
       self.name = name

<span class="hljs-class"><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">Child</span>(<span class="hljs-params">Parent</span>):</span>
   <span class="hljs-comment"># Constructor</span>
   <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">__init__</span>(<span class="hljs-params">self, name, age</span>):</span>
       <span class="hljs-string">'''
       In Python 3.x, we can also use super().__init__(name)
       '''</span>
       <span class="hljs-built_in">super</span>(Child, self).__init__(name)
       self.age = age

   <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">display</span>(<span class="hljs-params">self</span>):</span>
      <span class="hljs-comment"># Note that Parent.name cant be used </span>
      <span class="hljs-comment"># here since super() is used in the constructor</span>
      <span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(self.name, self.age)

<span class="hljs-comment"># Driver Code</span>
obj = Child(<span class="hljs-string">"Interviewbit"</span>, <span class="hljs-number">6</span>)
obj.display()</code></pre>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="are-access-specifiers-used-in-python">
          <h3>42. Are access specifiers used in python?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>Python does not make use of access specifiers specifically like private, public, protected, etc. However, it does not derive this from any variables. It has the concept of imitating the behaviour of variables by making use of a single (protected) or double underscore (private) as prefixed to the variable names. By default, the variables without prefixed underscores are public.</p><p><strong>Example:</strong></p><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-comment"># to demonstrate access specifiers</span>
<span class="hljs-class"><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">InterviewbitEmployee</span>:</span>

    <span class="hljs-comment"># protected members</span>
    _emp_name = <span class="hljs-literal">None</span>
    _age = <span class="hljs-literal">None</span>

    <span class="hljs-comment"># private members</span>
    __branch = <span class="hljs-literal">None</span>

    <span class="hljs-comment"># constructor</span>
    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">__init__</span>(<span class="hljs-params">self, emp_name, age, branch</span>):</span>
         self._emp_name = emp_name
         self._age = age
         self.__branch = branch

    <span class="hljs-comment">#public member</span>
    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">display</span>():</span>
        <span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(self._emp_name +<span class="hljs-string">" "</span>+self._age+<span class="hljs-string">" "</span>+self.__branch)</code></pre>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="is-it-possible-to-call-parent-class-without-its-instance-creation">
          <h3>43. Is it possible to call parent class without its instance creation?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>Yes, it is possible if the base class is instantiated by other child classes or if the base class is a static method.</p>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="how-to-create-empty-class-in-python">
          <h3>44. How is an empty class created in python?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>An empty class does not have any members defined in it. It is created by using the pass keyword (the pass command does nothing in python). We can create objects for this class outside the class.<br>For example-</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-class"><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">EmptyClassDemo</span>:</span>
   <span class="hljs-keyword">pass</span>
obj=EmptyClassDemo()
obj.name=<span class="hljs-string">"Interviewbit"</span>
<span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"Name created= "</span>,obj.name)</code></pre><p><strong>Output:</strong><br>Name created = Interviewbit</p>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="difference-between-new-and-override">
          <h3>45. Differentiate between new and override modifiers.</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>The new modifier is used to instruct the compiler to use the new implementation and not the base class function. The Override modifier is useful for overriding a base class function inside the child class.</p>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="why-is-finalize-method-used">
          <h3>46. Why is finalize used?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>Finalize method is used for freeing up the unmanaged resources and clean up before the garbage collection method is invoked. This helps in performing memory management tasks.</p>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="what-is-init-method-in-python">
          <h3>47. What is init method in python?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>The <strong>init</strong> method works similarly to the constructors in Java. The method is run as soon as an object is instantiated. It is useful for initializing any attributes or default behaviour of the object at the time of instantiation.<br>For example:</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-class"><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">InterviewbitEmployee</span>:</span>

   <span class="hljs-comment"># init method / constructor</span>
   <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">__init__</span>(<span class="hljs-params">self, emp_name</span>):</span>
       self.emp_name = emp_name

   <span class="hljs-comment"># introduce method</span>
   <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">introduce</span>(<span class="hljs-params">self</span>):</span>
       <span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(<span class="hljs-string">'Hello, I am '</span>, self.emp_name)

emp = InterviewbitEmployee(<span class="hljs-string">'Mr Employee'</span>)    <span class="hljs-comment"># __init__ method is called here and initializes the object name with "Mr Employee"</span>
emp.introduce()</code></pre>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="how-will-you-check-if-a-class-is-a-child-of-another-class">
          <h3>48. How will you check if a class is a child of another class?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>This is done by using a method called <strong>issubclass()</strong> provided by python. The method tells us if any class is a child of another class by returning true or false accordingly.<br><strong>For example:</strong></p><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-class"><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">Parent</span>(<span class="hljs-params"><span class="hljs-built_in">object</span></span>):</span>
   <span class="hljs-keyword">pass</span>

<span class="hljs-class"><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">Child</span>(<span class="hljs-params">Parent</span>):</span>
   <span class="hljs-keyword">pass</span>

<span class="hljs-comment"># Driver Code</span>
<span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(<span class="hljs-built_in">issubclass</span>(Child, Parent))    <span class="hljs-comment">#True</span>
<span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(<span class="hljs-built_in">issubclass</span>(Parent, Child))    <span class="hljs-comment">#False</span></code></pre><ul><li>We can check if an object is an instance of a class by making use of <strong>isinstance()</strong> method:</li></ul><pre><code class="language-python hljs">obj1 = Child()
obj2 = Parent()
<span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(<span class="hljs-built_in">isinstance</span>(obj2, Child))    <span class="hljs-comment">#False </span>
<span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(<span class="hljs-built_in">isinstance</span>(obj2, Parent))   <span class="hljs-comment">#True </span></code></pre>
          </article>
        </section>

  </div>
  <div id="python-pandas">
    <h2>Python Pandas Interview Questions</h2>

        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="pandas-in-python">
          <h3>49. What do you know about pandas?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <ul>
<li>Pandas is an open-source, python-based library used in data manipulation applications requiring high performance. The name is derived from Panel Data having multidimensional data. This was developed in 2008 by Wes McKinney and was developed for data analysis.</li>
<li>Pandas are useful in performing 5 major steps of data analysis - Load the data, clean/manipulate it, prepare it, model it, and analyze the data.</li>
</ul>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="define-pandas-dataframe">
          <h3>50. Define pandas dataframe.</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>A dataframe is a 2D mutable and tabular structure for representing data labelled with axes - rows and columns.<br><strong>The syntax for creating dataframe:</strong></p><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> pandas <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> pd
dataframe = pd.DataFrame( data, index, columns, dtype)</code></pre><p>where:</p><ul>
<li>data - Represents various forms like series, map, ndarray, lists, dict etc.</li>
<li>index - Optional argument that represents an index to row labels.</li>
<li>columns - Optional argument for column labels.</li>
<li>Dtype - the data type of each column. Again optional.</li>
</ul>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="merge-pandas-dataframes">
          <h3>51. How will you combine different pandas dataframes?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>The dataframes can be combines using the below approaches:</p><ul><li>
<strong>append() method</strong>: This is used to stack the dataframes horizontally. Syntax:</li></ul><pre><code class="language-python hljs">df1.append(df2)</code></pre><ul><li>
<strong>concat() method: </strong>This is used to stack dataframes vertically. This is best used when the dataframes have the same columns and similar fields. Syntax:</li></ul><pre><code class="language-python hljs">pd.concat([df1, df2]) </code></pre><ul><li>
<strong>join() method: </strong>This is used for extracting data from various dataframes having one or more common columns.</li></ul><pre><code class="language-python hljs">df1.join(df2)</code></pre>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="create-series-from-dictionary-in-pandas">
          <h3>52. Can you create a series from the dictionary object in pandas?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>One dimensional array capable of storing different data types is called a series. We can create pandas series from a dictionary object as shown below:</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> pandas <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> pd
dict_info = {<span class="hljs-string">'key1'</span> : <span class="hljs-number">2.0</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'key2'</span> : <span class="hljs-number">3.1</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'key3'</span> : <span class="hljs-number">2.2</span>}
series_obj = pd.Series(dict_info)
<span class="hljs-built_in">print</span> (series_obj)
Output:
x     <span class="hljs-number">2.0</span>
y     <span class="hljs-number">3.1</span>
z     <span class="hljs-number">2.2</span>
dtype: float64</code></pre><p>If an index is not specified in the input method, then the keys of the dictionaries are sorted in ascending order for constructing the index. In case the index is passed, then values of the index label will be extracted from the dictionary.</p>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="identifying-and-dealing-with-missing-values-in-a-dataframe">
          <h3>53. How will you identify and deal with missing values in a dataframe?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>We can identify if a dataframe has missing values by using the isnull() and isna() methods.</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs">missing_data_count=df.isnull().<span class="hljs-built_in">sum</span>()</code></pre><p>We can handle missing values by either replacing the values in the column with 0 as follows:</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs">df[column_name].fillna(<span class="hljs-number">0</span>)</code></pre><p>Or by replacing it with the mean value of the column</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs">df[column_name] = df[column_name].fillna((df[column_name].mean()))</code></pre>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="reindexing-in-pandas-dataframe">
          <h3>54. What do you understand by reindexing in pandas?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>Reindexing is the process of conforming a dataframe to a new index with optional filling logic. If the values are missing in the previous index, then NaN/NA is placed in the location. A new object is returned unless a new index is produced that is equivalent to the current one. The copy value is set to False. This is also used for changing the index of rows and columns in the dataframe.</p>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="how-to-add-new-column-to-pandas-dataframe">
          <h3>55. How to add new column to pandas dataframe?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>A new column can be added to a pandas dataframe as follows:</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> pandas <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> pd
data_info = {<span class="hljs-string">'first'</span> : pd.Series([<span class="hljs-number">1</span>, <span class="hljs-number">2</span>, <span class="hljs-number">3</span>], index=[<span class="hljs-string">'a'</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'b'</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'c'</span>]),
       <span class="hljs-string">'second'</span> : pd.Series([<span class="hljs-number">1</span>, <span class="hljs-number">2</span>, <span class="hljs-number">3</span>, <span class="hljs-number">4</span>], index=[<span class="hljs-string">'a'</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'b'</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'c'</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'d'</span>])}

df = pd.DataFrame(data_info)
<span class="hljs-comment">#To add new column third</span>
df[<span class="hljs-string">'third'</span>]=pd.Series([<span class="hljs-number">10</span>,<span class="hljs-number">20</span>,<span class="hljs-number">30</span>],index=[<span class="hljs-string">'a'</span>,<span class="hljs-string">'b'</span>,<span class="hljs-string">'c'</span>])
<span class="hljs-built_in">print</span> (df)
<span class="hljs-comment">#To add new column fourth</span>
df[<span class="hljs-string">'fourth'</span>]=df[<span class="hljs-string">'first'</span>]+info[<span class="hljs-string">'third'</span>]
<span class="hljs-built_in">print</span> (df)    </code></pre>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="how-will-you-delete-indices-rows-and-columns-from-a-dataframe">
          <h3>56. How will you delete indices, rows and columns from a dataframe?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p><strong>To delete an Index:</strong></p><ul>
<li>Execute <code>del df.index.name</code> for removing the index by name.</li>
<li>Alternatively, the <code>df.index.name</code> can be assigned to None.</li>
<li>For example, if you have the below dataframe:</li>
</ul><pre><code class="language-python hljs">                Column <span class="hljs-number">1</span>
   Names
   John               <span class="hljs-number">1</span>
   Jack               <span class="hljs-number">2</span>
   Judy               <span class="hljs-number">3</span>
   Jim                <span class="hljs-number">4</span></code></pre><ul><li>To drop the index name Names:</li></ul><pre><code class="language-python hljs">df.index.name = <span class="hljs-literal">None</span>
<span class="hljs-comment"># Or run the below:</span>
<span class="hljs-comment"># del df.index.name</span>
<span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(df)
        Column <span class="hljs-number">1</span>
John          <span class="hljs-number">1</span>
Jack          <span class="hljs-number">2</span>
Judy          <span class="hljs-number">3</span>
Jim           <span class="hljs-number">4</span></code></pre><p><strong>To delete row/column from dataframe:</strong></p><ul>
<li>
<code>drop()</code> method is used to delete row/column from dataframe.</li>
<li>The axis argument is passed to the drop method where if the value is 0, it indicates to drop/delete a row and if 1 it has to drop the column.</li>
<li>Additionally, we can try to delete the rows/columns in place by setting the value of inplace to True. This makes sure that the job is done without the need for reassignment.</li>
<li>The duplicate values from the row/column can be deleted by using the <code>drop_duplicates()</code> method.</li>
</ul><figure class="image image_resized" style="width:75%;"><img data-src="https://s3.ap-south-1.amazonaws.com/myinterviewtrainer-domestic/public_assets/assets/000/000/937/original/delete_rowcolumn_from_dataframe.jpg?1629989310" class="lazy-elem"></figure>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="get-items-of-series-at-that-are-not-available-in-another-series-b">
          <h3>57. Can you get items of series A that are not available in another series B?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>This can be achieved by using the <code>~</code> (not/negation symbol) and <code>isin()</code> method as shown below.</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> pandas <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> pd
df1 = pd.Series([<span class="hljs-number">2</span>, <span class="hljs-number">4</span>, <span class="hljs-number">8</span>, <span class="hljs-number">10</span>, <span class="hljs-number">12</span>])
df2 = pd.Series([<span class="hljs-number">8</span>, <span class="hljs-number">12</span>, <span class="hljs-number">10</span>, <span class="hljs-number">15</span>, <span class="hljs-number">16</span>])
df1=df1[~df1.isin(df2)]
<span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(df1)
<span class="hljs-string">"""
Output:
0    2
1    4
dtype: int64
"""</span></code></pre>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="get-the-items-that-are-not-common-to-both-the-given-series-a-and-b">
          <h3>58. How will you get the items that are not common to both the given series A and B?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>We can achieve this by first performing the union of both series, then taking the intersection of both series. Then we follow the approach of getting items of union that are not there in the list of the intersection.</p><figure class="image image_resized" style="width:75%;"><img data-src="https://s3.ap-south-1.amazonaws.com/myinterviewtrainer-domestic/public_assets/assets/000/000/938/original/get_the_items_that_are_not_common_to_both_the_given_series_A_and_B.jpg?1629989593" class="lazy-elem"></figure><p>The following code demonstrates this:</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> pandas <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> pd
<span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> numpy <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> np
df1 = pd.Series([<span class="hljs-number">2</span>, <span class="hljs-number">4</span>, <span class="hljs-number">5</span>, <span class="hljs-number">8</span>, <span class="hljs-number">10</span>])
df2 = pd.Series([<span class="hljs-number">8</span>, <span class="hljs-number">10</span>, <span class="hljs-number">13</span>, <span class="hljs-number">15</span>, <span class="hljs-number">17</span>])
p_union = pd.Series(np.union1d(df1, df2))  <span class="hljs-comment"># union of series</span>
p_intersect = pd.Series(np.intersect1d(df1, df2))  <span class="hljs-comment"># intersection of series</span>
unique_elements = p_union[~p_union.isin(p_intersect)]
<span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(unique_elements)
<span class="hljs-string">"""
Output:
0     2
1     4
2     5
5    13
6    15
7    17
dtype: int64
"""</span></code></pre>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="while-importing-data-from-different-sources-can-the-pandas-library-recognize-dates">
          <h3>59. While importing data from different sources, can the pandas library recognize dates?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>Yes, they can, but with some bit of help. We need to add the parse_dates argument while we are reading data from the sources. Consider an example where we read data from a CSV file, we may encounter different date-time formats that are not readable by the pandas library. In this case, pandas provide flexibility to build our custom date parser with the help of lambda functions as shown below:</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> pandas <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> pd
<span class="hljs-keyword">from</span> datetime <span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> datetime
dateparser = <span class="hljs-keyword">lambda</span> date_val: datetime.strptime(date_val, <span class="hljs-string">'%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S'</span>)
df = pd.read_csv(<span class="hljs-string">"some_file.csv"</span>, parse_dates=[<span class="hljs-string">'datetime_column'</span>], date_parser=dateparser)</code></pre>
          </article>
        </section>

  <div id="python-numpy">
    <h2>Numpy Interview Questions</h2>

        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="what-is-numpy">
          <h3>60. What do you understand by NumPy?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>NumPy is one of the most popular, easy-to-use, versatile, open-source, python-based, general-purpose package that is used for processing arrays. NumPy is short for NUMerical PYthon. This is very famous for its highly optimized tools that result in high performance and powerful N-Dimensional array processing feature that is designed explicitly to work on complex arrays. Due to its popularity and powerful performance and its flexibility to perform various operations like trigonometric operations, algebraic and statistical computations, it is most commonly used in performing scientific computations and various broadcasting functions. The following image shows the applications of NumPy:</p><figure class="image"><img data-src="https://s3.ap-south-1.amazonaws.com/myinterviewtrainer-domestic/public_assets/assets/000/000/939/original/uses_of_numpy.jpg?1629989876" class="lazy-elem"></figure>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="advantages-of-using-numpy-arrays-over-python-lists">
          <h3>61. How are NumPy arrays advantageous over python lists?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <ul>
<li>The list data structure of python is very highly efficient and is capable of performing various functions. But, they have severe limitations when it comes to the computation of vectorized operations which deals with element-wise multiplication and addition. The python lists also require the information regarding the type of every element which results in overhead as type dispatching code gets executes every time any operation is performed on any element. This is where the NumPy arrays come into the picture as all the limitations of python lists are handled in NumPy arrays.</li>
<li>Additionally, as the size of the NumPy arrays increases, NumPy becomes around 30x times faster than the Python List. This is because the Numpy arrays are densely packed in the memory due to their homogenous nature. This ensures the memory free up is also faster.</li>
</ul>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="steps-to-create-1d-2d-and-3d-arrays-using-numpy">
          <h3>62. What are the steps to create 1D, 2D and 3D arrays?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <ul><li><strong>1D array creation:</strong></li></ul><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> numpy <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> np
one_dimensional_list = [<span class="hljs-number">1</span>,<span class="hljs-number">2</span>,<span class="hljs-number">4</span>]
one_dimensional_arr = np.array(one_dimensional_list)
<span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"1D array is : "</span>,one_dimensional_arr) </code></pre><ul><li><strong>2D array creation:</strong></li></ul><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> numpy <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> np
two_dimensional_list=[[<span class="hljs-number">1</span>,<span class="hljs-number">2</span>,<span class="hljs-number">3</span>],[<span class="hljs-number">4</span>,<span class="hljs-number">5</span>,<span class="hljs-number">6</span>]]
two_dimensional_arr = np.array(two_dimensional_list)
<span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"2D array is : "</span>,two_dimensional_arr)</code></pre><ul><li><strong>3D array creation:</strong></li></ul><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> numpy <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> np
three_dimensional_list=[[[<span class="hljs-number">1</span>,<span class="hljs-number">2</span>,<span class="hljs-number">3</span>],[<span class="hljs-number">4</span>,<span class="hljs-number">5</span>,<span class="hljs-number">6</span>],[<span class="hljs-number">7</span>,<span class="hljs-number">8</span>,<span class="hljs-number">9</span>]]]
three_dimensional_arr = np.array(three_dimensional_list)
<span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"3D array is : "</span>,three_dimensional_arr) </code></pre><ul><li>
<strong>ND array creation: </strong>This can be achieved by giving the ndmin attribute. The below example demonstrates the creation of a 6D array:</li></ul><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> numpy <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> np
ndArray = np.array([<span class="hljs-number">1</span>, <span class="hljs-number">2</span>, <span class="hljs-number">3</span>, <span class="hljs-number">4</span>], ndmin=<span class="hljs-number">6</span>)
<span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(ndArray)
<span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(<span class="hljs-string">'Dimensions of array:'</span>, ndArray.ndim)</code></pre>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="delete-the-second-column-and-replace-the-column-with-a new-column-value-from-given-numpy-array">
          <h3>63. You are given a numpy array and a new column as inputs. How will you delete the second column and replace the column with a new column value?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p><strong>Example:</strong><br>Given array:</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs">[[<span class="hljs-number">35</span> <span class="hljs-number">53</span> <span class="hljs-number">63</span>]
[<span class="hljs-number">72</span> <span class="hljs-number">12</span> <span class="hljs-number">22</span>]
[<span class="hljs-number">43</span> <span class="hljs-number">84</span> <span class="hljs-number">56</span>]]</code></pre><p>New Column values:</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs">[
   <span class="hljs-number">20</span>
   <span class="hljs-number">30</span>
   <span class="hljs-number">40</span>
]</code></pre><p><strong>Solution:</strong></p><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> numpy <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> np
<span class="hljs-comment">#inputs</span>
inputArray = np.array([[<span class="hljs-number">35</span>,<span class="hljs-number">53</span>,<span class="hljs-number">63</span>],[<span class="hljs-number">72</span>,<span class="hljs-number">12</span>,<span class="hljs-number">22</span>],[<span class="hljs-number">43</span>,<span class="hljs-number">84</span>,<span class="hljs-number">56</span>]])
new_col = np.array([[<span class="hljs-number">20</span>,<span class="hljs-number">30</span>,<span class="hljs-number">40</span>]])
<span class="hljs-comment"># delete 2nd column</span>
arr = np.delete(inputArray , <span class="hljs-number">1</span>, axis = <span class="hljs-number">1</span>)
<span class="hljs-comment">#insert new_col to array</span>
arr = np.insert(arr , <span class="hljs-number">1</span>, new_col, axis = <span class="hljs-number">1</span>)
<span class="hljs-built_in">print</span> (arr) </code></pre>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="loading-a-text-file-data-using-numpy">
          <h3>64. How will you efficiently load data from a text file?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>We can use the method <code>numpy.loadtxt()</code> which can automatically read the files header and footer lines and the comments if any.</p><p>This method is highly efficient and even if this method feels less efficient, then the data should be represented in a more efficient format such as CSV etc. Various alternatives can be considered depending on the version of NumPy used.</p><p>Following are the file formats that are supported:</p><ul>
<li>Text files: These files are generally very slow, huge but portable and are human-readable.</li>
<li>Raw binary: This file does not have any metadata and is not portable. But they are fast.</li>
<li>Pickle: These are borderline slow and portable but depends on the NumPy versions.</li>
<li>HDF5: This is known as the High-Powered Kitchen Sink format which supports both PyTables and h5py format.</li>
<li>.npy: This is NumPy's native binary data format which is extremely simple, efficient and portable.</li>
</ul>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="how-will-you-read-csv-data-into-an-array-in-numpy">
          <h3>65. How will you read CSV data into an array in NumPy?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>This can be achieved by using the genfromtxt() method by setting the delimiter as a comma.</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-keyword">from</span> numpy <span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> genfromtxt
csv_data = genfromtxt(<span class="hljs-string">'sample_file.csv'</span>, delimiter=<span class="hljs-string">','</span>)</code></pre>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="how-will-you-sort-the-array-based-on-the-nth-column">
          <h3>66. How will you sort the array based on the Nth column?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>For example, consider an array arr.</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs">arr = np.array([[<span class="hljs-number">8</span>, <span class="hljs-number">3</span>, <span class="hljs-number">2</span>],
          [<span class="hljs-number">3</span>, <span class="hljs-number">6</span>, <span class="hljs-number">5</span>],
          [<span class="hljs-number">6</span>, <span class="hljs-number">1</span>, <span class="hljs-number">4</span>]])</code></pre><p>Let us try to sort the rows by the 2nd column so that we get:</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs">[[<span class="hljs-number">6</span>, <span class="hljs-number">1</span>, <span class="hljs-number">4</span>],
[<span class="hljs-number">8</span>, <span class="hljs-number">3</span>, <span class="hljs-number">2</span>],
[<span class="hljs-number">3</span>, <span class="hljs-number">6</span>, <span class="hljs-number">5</span>]]</code></pre><p>We can do this by using the sort() method in numpy as:</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> numpy <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> np
arr = np.array([[<span class="hljs-number">8</span>, <span class="hljs-number">3</span>, <span class="hljs-number">2</span>],
          [<span class="hljs-number">3</span>, <span class="hljs-number">6</span>, <span class="hljs-number">5</span>],
          [<span class="hljs-number">6</span>, <span class="hljs-number">1</span>, <span class="hljs-number">4</span>]])
<span class="hljs-comment">#sort the array using np.sort</span>
arr = np.sort(arr.view(<span class="hljs-string">'i8,i8,i8'</span>),
       order=[<span class="hljs-string">'f1'</span>],
       axis=<span class="hljs-number">0</span>).view(np.<span class="hljs-built_in">int</span>)</code></pre><p>We can also perform sorting and that too inplace sorting by doing:</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs">arr.view(<span class="hljs-string">'i8,i8,i8'</span>).sort(order=[<span class="hljs-string">'f1'</span>], axis=<span class="hljs-number">0</span>)</code></pre>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="how-will-you-find-the-nearest-value-in-a-given-numpy-array">
          <h3>67. How will you find the nearest value in a given numpy array?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>We can use the argmin() method of numpy as shown below:</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> numpy <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> np
<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">find_nearest_value</span>(<span class="hljs-params">arr, value</span>):</span>
   arr = np.asarray(arr)
   idx = (np.<span class="hljs-built_in">abs</span>(arr - value)).argmin()
   <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> arr[idx]
<span class="hljs-comment">#Driver code</span>
arr = np.array([ <span class="hljs-number">0.21169</span>,  <span class="hljs-number">0.61391</span>, <span class="hljs-number">0.6341</span>, <span class="hljs-number">0.0131</span>, <span class="hljs-number">0.16541</span>,  <span class="hljs-number">0.5645</span>,  <span class="hljs-number">0.5742</span>])
value = <span class="hljs-number">0.52</span>
<span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(find_nearest_value(arr, value)) <span class="hljs-comment"># Prints 0.5645</span></code></pre>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="reverse-the-numpy-array-using-one-line-of-code">
          <h3>68. How will you reverse the numpy array using one line of code?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>This can be done as shown in the following:</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs">reversed_array = arr[::-<span class="hljs-number">1</span>]</code></pre><p>where <strong>arr</strong> = original given array, reverse_array is the resultant after reversing all elements in the input.</p>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="find-the-shape-of-any-given-numpy-array">
          <h3>69. How will you find the shape of any given NumPy array?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>We can use the shape attribute of the numpy array to find the shape.              (<span class="hljs-string">"x5"</span>,<span class="hljs-string">"x6"</span>, <span class="hljs-string">"x7"</span>,<span class="hljs-string">"x8"</span> )])
arr_one_dim = np.array([<span class="hljs-number">3</span>,<span class="hljs-number">2</span>,<span class="hljs-number">4</span>,<span class="hljs-number">5</span>,<span class="hljs-number">6</span>])

  <div id="python-libraries">
    <h2>Python Libraries Interview Questions</h2>

        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="modules-and-packages-in-python">
          <h3>70. Differentiate between a package and a module in python.</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>The module is a single python file. A module can import other modules (other python files) as objects. Whereas, a package is the folder/directory where different sub-packages and the modules reside.</p><p>A python module is created by saving a file with the extension of <code>.py</code>. This file will have classes and functions that are reusable in the code as well as across modules.</p><p>A python package is created by following the below steps:</p><ul>
<li>Create a directory and give a valid name that represents its operation.</li>
<li>Place modules of one kind in this directory.</li>
<li>Create <code>__init__.py</code> file in this directory. This lets python know the directory we created is a package. The contents of this package can be imported across different modules in other packages to reuse the functionality.</li>
</ul>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="python-built-in-modules">
          <h3>71. What are some of the most commonly used built-in modules in Python?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>Python modules are the files having python code which can be functions, variables or classes. These go by .py extension. The most commonly available built-in modules are:</p><ul>
<li>os</li>
<li>math</li>
<li>sys</li>
<li>random</li>
<li>re</li>
<li>datetime</li>
<li>JSON</li>
</ul>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="lambda-functions-in-python">
          <h3>72. What are lambda functions?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>Lambda functions are generally inline, anonymous functions represented by a single expression. They are used for creating function objects during runtime. They can accept any number of parameters. They are usually used where functions are required only for a short period. They can be used as:</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs">mul_func = <span class="hljs-keyword">lambda</span> x,y : x*y
<span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(mul_func(<span class="hljs-number">6</span>, <span class="hljs-number">4</span>))
<span class="hljs-comment"># Output: 24</span></code></pre>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="generating-random-number-list-in-python">
          <h3>73. How can you generate random numbers?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>Python provides a module called random using which we can generate random numbers.</p><ul><li>We have to import a random module and call the <code>random()</code> method as shown below:<ul><li>The random() method generates float values lying between 0 and 1 randomly.</li></ul>
</li></ul><pre><code class="language-python hljs"> <span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> random
 <span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(random.random())</code></pre><ul><li>To generate customised random numbers between specified ranges, we can use the <code>randrange()</code> method<br>Syntax: <code>randrange(beginning, end, step)</code><br>For example:</li></ul><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> random
<span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(random.randrange(<span class="hljs-number">5</span>,<span class="hljs-number">100</span>,<span class="hljs-number">2</span>))</code></pre>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="check-if-all-characters-in-the-given-string-is-alphanumeric">
          <h3>74. Can you easily check if all characters in the given string is alphanumeric?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>This can be easily done by making use of the isalnum() method that returns true in case the string has only alphanumeric characters.</p><p>For Example -</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-string">"abdc1321"</span>.isalnum() <span class="hljs-comment">#Output: True</span>
<span class="hljs-string">"xyz@123$"</span>.isalnum() <span class="hljs-comment">#Output: False</span></code></pre><p>Another way is to use <code>match()</code> method from the re (regex) module as shown:</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> re
<span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(<span class="hljs-built_in">bool</span>(re.match(<span class="hljs-string">'[A-Za-z0-9]+$'</span>,<span class="hljs-string">'abdc1321'</span>))) <span class="hljs-comment"># Output: True</span>
<span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(<span class="hljs-built_in">bool</span>(re.match(<span class="hljs-string">'[A-Za-z0-9]+$'</span>,<span class="hljs-string">'xyz@123$'</span>))) <span class="hljs-comment"># Output: False</span></code></pre>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="pickling-vs-unpickling">
          <h3>75. What are the differences between pickling and unpickling?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>Pickling is the conversion of python objects to binary form. Whereas, unpickling is the conversion of binary form data to python objects. The pickled objects are used for storing in disks or external memory locations. Unpickled objects are used for getting the data back as python objects upon which processing can be done in python.</p><p>Python provides a <code>pickle</code> module for achieving this. Pickling uses the <code>pickle.dump()</code> method to dump python objects into disks. Unpickling uses the <code>pickle.load()</code> method to get back the data as python objects.</p><figure class="image"><img data-src="https://s3.ap-south-1.amazonaws.com/myinterviewtrainer-domestic/public_assets/assets/000/000/940/original/differences_between_pickling_and_unpickling.jpg?1629992411" class="lazy-elem"></figure>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="global-interpreter-lock">
          <h3>76. Define GIL.</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>GIL stands for Global Interpreter Lock. This is a mutex used for limiting access to python objects and aids in effective thread synchronization by avoiding deadlocks. GIL helps in achieving multitasking (and not parallel computing). The following diagram represents how GIL works.</p><figure class="image image_resized" style="width:75%;"><img data-src="https://s3.ap-south-1.amazonaws.com/myinterviewtrainer-domestic/public_assets/assets/000/000/941/original/Global_Interpreter_Lock.jpg?1629992761" class="lazy-elem"></figure><p>Based on the above diagram, there are three threads. First Thread acquires the GIL first and starts the I/O execution. When the I/O operations are done, thread 1 releases the acquired GIL which is then taken up by the second thread. The process repeats and the GIL are used by different threads alternatively until the threads have completed their execution. The threads not having the GIL lock goes into the waiting state and resumes execution only when it acquires the lock.</p>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="define-pythonpath">
          <h3>77. Define PYTHONPATH.</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>It is an environment variable used for incorporating additional directories during the import of a module or a package. PYTHONPATH is used for checking if the imported packages or modules are available in the existing directories. Not just that, the interpreter uses this environment variable to identify which module needs to be loaded.</p>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="python-pip">
          <h3>78. Define PIP.</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>PIP stands for Python Installer Package. As the name indicates, it is used for installing different python modules. It is a command-line tool providing a seamless interface for installing different python modules. It searches over the internet for the package and installs them into the working directory without the need for any interaction with the user. The syntax for this is:</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs">pip install &lt;package_name&gt;</code></pre>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="tools-for-identifying-bugs-and-performing-static-analysis-in-python">
          <h3>79. Are there any tools for identifying bugs and performing static analysis in python?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>Yes, there are tools like PyChecker and Pylint which are used as static analysis and linting tools respectively. PyChecker helps find bugs in python source code files and raises alerts for code issues and their complexity. Pylint checks for the modules coding standards and supports different plugins to enable custom features to meet this requirement.</p>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="difference-between-deep-and-shallow-copies">
          <h3>80. Differentiate between deep and shallow copies.</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <ul>
<li>Shallow copy does the task of creating new objects storing references of original elements. This does not undergo recursion to create copies of nested objects. It just copies the reference details of nested objects.</li>
<li>Deep copy creates an independent and new copy of an object and even copies all the nested objects of the original element recursively.</li>
</ul>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="python-main-function-how-do-you-invoke-it">
          <h3>81. What is main function in python? How do you invoke it?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>In the world of programming languages, the main is considered as an entry point of execution for a program. But in python, it is known that the interpreter serially interprets the file line-by-line. This means that python does not provide <code>main()</code> function explicitly. But this doesn't mean that we cannot simulate the execution of main. This can be done by defining user-defined <code>main()</code> function and by using the <code>__name__</code> property of python file. This <code>__name__</code> variable is a special built-in variable that points to the name of the current module. This can be done as shown below:</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">main</span>():</span>
   <span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"Hi Interviewbit!"</span>)
<span class="hljs-keyword">if</span> __name__==<span class="hljs-string">"__main__"</span>:
   main()</code></pre>
          </article>
        </section>

  </div>
  <div id="python-programs">
    <h2>Python Programming Examples</h2>

        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="write-python-function-which-takes-a-variable-number-of-arguments">
          <h3>82. Write python function which takes a variable number of arguments.</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>A function that takes variable arguments is called a function prototype. Syntax:</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">function_name</span>(<span class="hljs-params">*arg_list</span>)</span></code></pre><p>For example:</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">func</span>(<span class="hljs-params">*var</span>):</span>
   <span class="hljs-keyword">for</span> i <span class="hljs-keyword">in</span> var:
       <span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(i)
func(<span class="hljs-number">1</span>)
func(<span class="hljs-number">20</span>,<span class="hljs-number">1</span>,<span class="hljs-number">6</span>)</code></pre><p>The * in the function argument represents variable arguments in the function.</p>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="program-which-takes-a-sequence-of-numbers-and-check-if-all-numbers-are-unique">
          <h3>83. WAP (Write a program) which takes a sequence of numbers and check if all numbers are unique.</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>You can do this by converting the list to set by using set() method and comparing the length of this set with the length of the original list. If found equal, return True.</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">check_distinct</span>(<span class="hljs-params">data_list</span>):</span>
 <span class="hljs-keyword">if</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">len</span>(data_list) == <span class="hljs-built_in">len</span>(<span class="hljs-built_in">set</span>(data_list)):
   <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> <span class="hljs-literal">True</span>
 <span class="hljs-keyword">else</span>:
   <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> <span class="hljs-literal">False</span>;
<span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(check_distinct([<span class="hljs-number">1</span>,<span class="hljs-number">6</span>,<span class="hljs-number">5</span>,<span class="hljs-number">8</span>]))     <span class="hljs-comment">#Prints True</span>
<span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(check_distinct([<span class="hljs-number">2</span>,<span class="hljs-number">2</span>,<span class="hljs-number">5</span>,<span class="hljs-number">5</span>,<span class="hljs-number">7</span>,<span class="hljs-number">8</span>])) <span class="hljs-comment">#Prints False</span></code></pre>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="program-for-counting-the-number-of-every-character-of-a-given-text-file">
          <h3>84. Write a program for counting the number of every character of a given text file.</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>The idea is to use collections and pprint module as shown below:</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> collections
<span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> pprint
<span class="hljs-keyword">with</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">open</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"sample_file.txt"</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'r'</span>) <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> data:
 count_data = collections.Counter(data.read().upper())
 count_value = pprint.pformat(count_data)
<span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(count_value)</code></pre>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="program-to-check-and-return-the-pairs-of-a-given-array-a-whose-sum-value-is-equal-to-a-target-value-n">
          <h3>85. Write a program to check and return the pairs of a given array A whose sum value is equal to a target value N.</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>This can be done easily by using the phenomenon of hashing. We can use a hash map to check for the current value of the array, x. If the map has the value of (N-x), then there is our pair.</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">print_pairs</span>(<span class="hljs-params">arr, N</span>):</span>
   <span class="hljs-comment"># hash set</span>
   hash_set = <span class="hljs-built_in">set</span>()

   <span class="hljs-keyword">for</span> i <span class="hljs-keyword">in</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">range</span>(<span class="hljs-number">0</span>, <span class="hljs-built_in">len</span>(arr)):
       val = N-arr[i]
       <span class="hljs-keyword">if</span> (val <span class="hljs-keyword">in</span> hash_set):    <span class="hljs-comment">#check if N-x is there in set, print the pair</span>
           <span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"Pairs "</span> + <span class="hljs-built_in">str</span>(arr[i]) + <span class="hljs-string">", "</span> + <span class="hljs-built_in">str</span>(val))
       hash_set.add(arr[i])

<span class="hljs-comment"># driver code</span>
arr = [<span class="hljs-number">1</span>, <span class="hljs-number">2</span>, <span class="hljs-number">40</span>, <span class="hljs-number">3</span>, <span class="hljs-number">9</span>, <span class="hljs-number">4</span>]
N = <span class="hljs-number">3</span>
print_pairs(arr, N)</code></pre>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="program-to-add-two-integers-greater-than-zero-without-using-the-plus-operator">
          <h3>86. Write a Program to add two integers &gt;0 without using the plus operator.</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>We can use bitwise operators to achieve this.</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">add_nums</span>(<span class="hljs-params">num1, num2</span>):</span>
   <span class="hljs-keyword">while</span> num2 != <span class="hljs-number">0</span>:
       data = num1 &amp; num2
       num1 = num1 ^ num2
       num2 = data &lt;&lt; <span class="hljs-number">1</span>
   <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> num1
<span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(add_nums(<span class="hljs-number">2</span>, <span class="hljs-number">10</span>))</code></pre>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="program-to-solve-the-given-equation-assuming-that-a-b-c-m-n-o-are-constants">
          <h3>87. Write a Program to solve the given equation assuming that a,b,c,m,n,o are constants:</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <pre><code class="language-python hljs">ax + by = c
mx + ny = o</code></pre><p>By solving the equation, we get:</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs">a, b, c, m, n, o = <span class="hljs-number">5</span>, <span class="hljs-number">9</span>, <span class="hljs-number">4</span>, <span class="hljs-number">7</span>, <span class="hljs-number">9</span>, <span class="hljs-number">4</span>
temp = a*n - b*m
<span class="hljs-keyword">if</span> n != <span class="hljs-number">0</span>:
   x = (c*n - b*o) / temp
   y = (a*o - m*c) / temp
   <span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(<span class="hljs-built_in">str</span>(x), <span class="hljs-built_in">str</span>(y))</code></pre>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="program-to-match-a-string-that-has-the-letter-a-followed-by-4-to-8-b">
          <h3>88. Write a Program to match a string that has the letter a followed by 4 to 8 &#39;bs.</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>We can use the re module of python to perform regex pattern comparison here.</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> re
<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">match_text</span>(<span class="hljs-params">txt_data</span>):</span>
       pattern = <span class="hljs-string">'ab{4,8}'</span>
       <span class="hljs-keyword">if</span> re.search(pattern,  txt_data):    <span class="hljs-comment">#search for pattern in txt_data</span>
           <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> <span class="hljs-string">'Match found'</span>
       <span class="hljs-keyword">else</span>:
           <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span>(<span class="hljs-string">'Match not found'</span>)
<span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(match_text(<span class="hljs-string">"abc"</span>))         <span class="hljs-comment">#prints Match not found</span>
<span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(match_text(<span class="hljs-string">"aabbbbbc"</span>))    <span class="hljs-comment">#prints Match found</span></code></pre>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="program-to-convert-date-from-yyyy-mm-dd-format-to-dd-mm-yyyy-format">
          <h3>89. Write a Program to convert date from yyyy-mm-dd format to dd-mm-yyyy format.</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>We can again use the re module to convert the date string as shown below:</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> re
<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">transform_date_format</span>(<span class="hljs-params">date</span>):</span>
   <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> re.sub(<span class="hljs-string">r'(\d{4})-(\d{1,2})-(\d{1,2})'</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'\\3-\\2-\\1'</span>, date)
date_input = <span class="hljs-string">"2021-08-01"</span>
<span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(transform_date_format(date_input))</code></pre><p>You can also use the datetime module as shown below:</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-keyword">from</span> datetime <span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> datetime
new_date = datetime.strptime(<span class="hljs-string">"2021-08-01"</span>, <span class="hljs-string">"%Y-%m-%d"</span>).strftime(<span class="hljs-string">"%d:%m:%Y"</span>)
<span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(new_data)</code></pre>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="program-to-merge-dictionaries-in-python">
          <h3>90. Write a Program to combine two different dictionaries. While combining, if you find the same keys, you can add the values of these same keys. Output the new dictionary</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>We can use the Counter method from the collections module</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-keyword">from</span> collections <span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> Counter
d1 = {<span class="hljs-string">'key1'</span>: <span class="hljs-number">50</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'key2'</span>: <span class="hljs-number">100</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'key3'</span>:<span class="hljs-number">200</span>}
d2 = {<span class="hljs-string">'key1'</span>: <span class="hljs-number">200</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'key2'</span>: <span class="hljs-number">100</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'key4'</span>:<span class="hljs-number">300</span>}
new_dict = Counter(d1) + Counter(d2)
<span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(new_dict)</code></pre>
          </article>
        </section>
        <section class="ibpage-article-header" id="access-the-dataset-of-publicly-shared-spreadsheet-in-csv-format-stored-in-google-drive">
          <h3>91. How will you access the dataset of a publicly shared spreadsheet in CSV format stored in Google Drive?</h3>
          <article class="ibpage-article">
            <p>We can use the StringIO module from the io module to read from the Google Drive link and then we can use the pandas library using the obtained data source.</p><pre><code class="language-python hljs"><span class="hljs-keyword">from</span> io <span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> StringIO
<span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> pandas
csv_link = <span class="hljs-string">"https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/..."</span>
data_source = StringIO.StringIO(requests.get(csv_link).content))
dataframe = pd.read_csv(data_source)
<span class="hljs-built_in">print</span>(dataframe.head())</code></pre><h3>Conclusion:</h3><p>In this article, we have seen commonly asked interview questions for a python developer.   <script>
    window.onload = function() {
      const waitTime = 45000;
      const accordion = document.querySelector('.moco-widget__header');
        const content = document.querySelector('.moco-widget__content');
        const label = document.querySelector('.moco-widget__label');

      function toggleActive() {
        accordion.classList.toggle('active');
        content.classList.toggle('active');
        if (content.style.maxHeight) {
          content.style.maxHeight = null;
          label.innerText = 'Know more';
        } else {
          content.style.maxHeight = '600px';
          label.innerText = 'Hide';
        }
      }

      const openWidget = setTimeout(()=>{
        toggleActive();
      }, waitTime)

      accordion.addEventListener('click', () => {
        clearTimeout(openWidget);
        toggleActive();
        if(accordion.className.includes('active')) {
          window.trackGaEvent('mock_assessment', 'banner_opened', window.location.pathname);
        }
      });

      window.trackGaEvent('mock_assessment', 'banner_shown', window.location.pathname);
    }
  </script>

      if (logged_in === 'false' && !disableAutoPropmt) {
        showPrompt();
      }
    };
  })(window);
</script>
